<p>and passions from the indulgence of which I was for</p>
<p>ever barred, then impotent envy and bitter indigna-</p>
<p>tion ﬁlled me with an insatiable thirst for vengeance.</p>
<p>I recollected my threat, and resolved that it should</p>
<p>be accomplished. I knew that I was preparing for</p>
<p>myself a deadly torture; but I was the slave, not the</p>
<p>master of an impulse, which I detested, yet could</p>
<p>not disobey. Yet when she died! — nay, then I was</p>
<p>not miserable. I had cast off all feeling, subdued</p>
<p>all anguish to riot in the excess of my despair. Evil</p>
<p>thenceforth became my good. Urged thus far, I had</p>
<p>no choice but to adapt my nature to an element</p>
<p>which I had willingly chosen. The completion of my</p>
<p>demoniacal design became an insatiable passion.</p>
<p>And now it is ended; there is my last victim!”</p>
<p>I was at ﬁrst touched by the expressions of his</p>
<p>misery; yet when I called to mind what Frankenstein</p>
<p>had said of his powers of eloquence and persua-</p>
<p>sion, and when I again cast my eyes on the lifeless</p>
<p>form of my friend, indignation was re-kindled within</p>
<p>me. “Wretch!” I said, “it is well that you come here to</p>
<p>whine over the desolation that you have made. You</p>
<p>throw a torch into a pile of buildings, and when they</p>
<p>are consumed you sit among the ruins, and lament</p>
<p>the fall. Hypocritical ﬁend! if he whom you mourn</p>
<p>still lived, still would he be the object, again would</p>
<p>he become the prey of your accursed vengeance.</p>
<p>It is not pity that you feel; you lament only because</p>
<p>the victim of your malignity is withdrawn from your</p>
<p>power.”</p>
<p>“Oh, it is not thus — not thus,” interrupted the</p>
<p>being; “yet such must be the impression conveyed</p>
<p>to you by what appears to be the purport of my</p>
<p>actions. Yet I seek not a fellow-feeling in my mis-</p>
<p>ery. No sympathy may I ever ﬁnd. When I ﬁrst</p>
<p>sought it, it was the love of virtue, the feelings of</p>
<p>happiness and affection with which my whole be-</p>
<p>ing overﬂowed, that I wished to be participated.</p>
<p>But now, that virtue has become to me a shadow,</p>
<p>and that happiness and affection are turned into</p>
<p>bitter and loathing despair, in what should I seek</p>
<p>for sympathy? I am content to suffer alone, while</p>
<p>my sufferings shall endure: when I die, I am well</p>
<p>satisﬁed that abhorrence and opprobrium should</p>
<p>load my memory. Once my fancy was soothed with</p>
<p>dreams of virtue, of fame, and of enjoyment. Once</p>
<p>I falsely hoped to meet with beings, who, pardoning</p>
<p>my outward form, would love me for the excellent</p>
<p>qualities which I was capable of bringing forth. I</p>
<p>was nourished with high thoughts of honour and</p>
<p>devotion. But now vice has degraded me beneath</p>
<p>the meanest animal. No crime, no mischief, no ma-</p>
<p>lignity, no misery, can be found comparable to mine.</p>
<p>When I call over the frightful catalogue of my deeds,</p>
<p>I cannot believe that I am he whose thoughts were</p>
<p>once ﬁlled with sublime and transcendant visions</p>
<p>of the beauty and the majesty of goodness. But it</p>
<p>is even so; the fallen angel becomes a malignant</p>
<p>devil. Yet even that enemy of God and man had</p>
<p>friends and associates in his desolation; I am quite</p>
<p>alone.</p>
<p>“You, who call Frankenstein your friend, seem to</p>
<p>have a knowledge of my crimes and his misfortunes.</p>
<p>But, in the detail which he gave you of them, he</p>
<p>could not sum up the hours and months of misery</p>
<p>which I endured, wasting in impotent passions. For</p>
<p>whilst I destroyed his hopes, I did not satisfy my own</p>
<p>desires. They were for ever ardent and craving;</p>
<p>still I desired love and fellowship, and I was still</p>
<p>spurned. Was there no injustice in this? Am I to</p>
<p>be thought the only criminal, when all human kind</p>
<p>sinned against me? Why do you not hate Felix, who</p>
<p>drove his friend from his door with contumely? Why</p>
<p>do you not execrate the rustic who sought to destroy</p>
<p>the saviour of his child? Nay, these are virtuous</p>
<p>and immaculate beings! I, the miserable and the</p>
<p>abandoned, am an abortion, to be spurned at, and</p>
<p>kicked, and trampled on. Even now my blood boils</p>
<p>at the recollection of this injustice.</p>
<p>“But it is true that I am a wretch. I have mur-</p>
<p>dered the lovely and the helpless; I have strangled</p>
<p>the innocent as they slept, and grasped to death</p>
<p>his throat who never injured me or any other living</p>
<p>thing. I have devoted my creator, the select spec-</p>
<p>imen of all that is worthy of love and admiration</p>
<p>among men, to misery; I have pursued him even to</p>
<p>that irremediable ruin. There he lies, white and cold</p>
<p>in death. You hate me; but your abhorrence cannot</p>
<p>equal that with which I regard myself. I look on the</p>
<p>hands which executed the deed; I think on the heart</p>
<p>in which the imagination of it was conceived, and</p>
<p>long for the moment when they will meet my eyes,</p>
<p>when it will haunt my thoughts, no more.</p>
<p>“Fear not that I shall be the instrument of fu-</p>
<p>ture mischief. My work is nearly complete. Neither</p>
<p>your’s nor any man’s death is needed to consum-</p>
<p>mate the series of my being, and accomplish that</p>
<p>which must be done; but it requires my own. Do</p>
<p>not think that I shall be slow to perform this sacri-</p>
<p>ﬁce. I shall quit your vessel on the ice-raft which</p>
<p>brought me hither, and shall seek the most northern</p>
<p>extremity of the globe; I shall collect my funeral pile,</p>
<p>and consume to ashes this miserable frame, that</p>
<p>its remains may afford no light to any curious and</p>
<p>unhallowed wretch, who would create such another</p>
<p>as I have been. I shall die. I shall no longer feel the</p>
<p>agonies which now consume me, or be the prey of</p>
<p>feelings unsatisﬁed, yet unquenched. He is dead</p>
<p>who called me into being; and when I shall be no</p>
<p>more, the very remembrance of us both will speed-</p>
<p>ily vanish. I shall no longer see the sun or stars,</p>
<p>or feel the winds play on my cheeks. Light, feeling,</p>
<p>and sense, will pass away; and in this condition</p>
<p>must I ﬁnd my happiness. Some years ago, when</p>
<p>the images which this world affords ﬁrst opened</p>
<p>upon me, when I felt the cheering warmth of sum-</p>
<p>mer, and heard the rustling of the leaves and the</p>
<p>chirping of the birds, and these were all to me, I</p>
<p>should have wept to die; now it is my only consola-</p>
<p>tion. Polluted by crimes, and torn by the bitterest</p>
<p>remorse, where can I ﬁnd rest but in death?</p>
<p>“Farewell! I leave you, and in you the last of</p>
<p>human kind whom these eyes will ever behold.</p>
<p>Farewell, Frankenstein! If thou wert yet alive, and</p>
<p>yet cherished a desire of revenge against me, it</p>
<p>would be better satiated in my life than in my de-</p>
<p>struction. But it was not so; thou didst seek my</p>
<p>extinction, that I might not cause greater wretched-</p>
<p>ness; and if yet, in some mode unknown to me,</p>
<p>thou hast not yet ceased to think and feel, thou</p>
<p>desirest not my life for my own misery. Blasted as</p>
<p>thou wert, my agony was still superior to thine; for</p>
<p>the bitter sting of remorse may not cease to rankle</p>
<p>in my wounds until death shall close them for ever.</p>
<p>“But soon,” he cried, with sad and solemn enthu-</p>
<p>siasm, “I shall die, and what I now feel be no longer</p>
<p>felt. Soon these burning miseries will be extinct. I</p>
<p>shall ascend my funeral pile triumphantly, and exult</p>
<p>in the agony of the torturing ﬂames. The light of</p>
<p>that conﬂagration will fade away; my ashes will be</p>
<p>swept into the sea by the winds. My spirit will sleep</p>
<p>in peace; or if it thinks, it will not surely think thus.</p>
<p>Farewell.”</p>
<p>He sprung from the cabin-window, as he said</p>
<p>this, upon the ice-raft which lay close to the vessel.</p>
<p>He was soon borne away by the waves, and lost in</p>
<p>darkness and distance.</p>
<p>THE END.</p>
